## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time through nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and potential external driving. Classical models include Duffing, van der Pol, and driven oscillators.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (periodically driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * x**2 + c3 * v (combined nonlinearities)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-cubed damping term)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric restoring force with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillator symmetry
- Position-velocity coupling terms like x**2 * v → amplitude-dependent damping (van der Pol type self-excitation)
- Cubic position term x**3 with same/opposite sign as linear term → hardening/softening spring behavior (Duffing)
- Sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) in acceleration → external periodic driving force
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v**3) in damping → energy dissipation that respects time-reversal symmetry of dissipation
- Product x * cos(c*t) → parametric excitation where stiffness is modulated periodically
- sin(c*x) as restoring force → finite-amplitude pendulum dynamics with bounded potential
- Velocity-independent terms determine the potential landscape; velocity-dependent terms control energy flow (gain/loss)
